  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_00df117e-6aca-4471-b442-e41588882b36'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText11333884137255904880" style="display:none">Football pro Mick Riley is an all-star, both on the field and in the bedroom. But a sexy, determinedly single mom just might be the one to throw him off his game...<br /><br />For years Mick has been taking full advantage of the life available to a pro athlete: fame, fortune, and a different girl in every city. But when he meets and beds confident, beautiful event planner Tara Lincoln, he wants much more than the typical one-night stand. Too bad Tara's not interested in getting to know football's most notorious playboy any better.<br /><br />As the single mother of a teenage son, the last thing Tara needs is the jet-set lifestyle of Mick Riley; even though their steamy and passionate one-night stand was unforgettable. Tara's life is complicated enough without being thrust into the spotlight as Mick's latest girl du jour. Tara played the game of love once and lost big, and she doesn't intend to put herself out there again, especially with a heartbreaker like Mick.<br /><br />But when Mick sets his mind to win, nothing will stop him. And he has the perfect play in mind.</span>

        $('edition_10041588').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_10041588').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});

            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });

<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Though it's been stated in the book (at separate points) that they're both 30, it's also been stated that Tara was 16 when she gave birth to Nathan, w<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Though it's been stated in the book (at separate points) that they're both 30, it's also been stated that Tara was 16 when she gave birth to Nathan, who's turning 15 -- so maybe Mick and Tara are the same age, but she's a few months older than him....?<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>

<div id="review_102932183" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102932183" />
    <a title="Auntee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/886675-auntee"><img alt="Auntee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1281897695p2/886675.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/102932183?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Auntee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Auntee" href="/user/show/886675-auntee">Auntee</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of erotic sports romance</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886675-auntee?shelf=jaci-burton">jaci-burton</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886675-auntee?shelf=erotic-romance">erotic-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886675-auntee?shelf=2011_reads">2011_reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886675-auntee?shelf=keepers">keepers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886675-auntee?shelf=i-ll-buy-for-the-cover-alone">i-ll-buy-for-the-cover-alone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886675-auntee?shelf=sports-romance">sports-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102932183" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3159668332665411470">Just in time for the upcoming Super Bowl is Jaci Burton's smokin' hot new release, <b>The Perfect Play</b>. And what a <i>perfect</i> sports romance it is! Starting with the gorgeous cover...<br/><br/><a href='http://s880.photobucket.com/albums/ac3/aunteecr/?action=view&current=jed-pants-1.jpg' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334961i/694116.jpg' alt='Photobucket' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>(C'mon, how can you resist that cover model?)<br/><br/>Things just get better after that. The story has an almost Cinderella-like feel to it. Mick Riley (30) is Mr. Tall (6 1/2 feet), Dark (black hair, blue-eyed) and Sexy (killer physique); a millionaire superstar quarterback for the San Francisco Sabers. Mick's a hard working </span>
  <span id="freeText3159668332665411470" style="display:none">Just in time for the upcoming Super Bowl is Jaci Burton's smokin' hot new release, <b>The Perfect Play</b>. And what a <i>perfect</i> sports romance it is! Starting with the gorgeous cover...<br><br><a href="http://s880.photobucket.com/albums/ac3/aunteecr/?action=view&amp;current=jed-pants-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334961i/694116.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>(C'mon, how can you resist that cover model?)<br><br>Things just get better after that. The story has an almost Cinderella-like feel to it. Mick Riley (30) is Mr. Tall (6 1/2 feet), Dark (black hair, blue-eyed) and Sexy (killer physique); a millionaire superstar quarterback for the San Francisco Sabers. Mick's a hard working athlete, but has never had to work for female companionship. Women flock to him, starlets, supermodels...you name it. His female sports agent (a real obnoxious, beautiful, power-hungry redhead named Elizabeth) wants nothing more than to see Mick on a red carpet escorting the hottest actress, or at some charity event with a beautiful model on his arm. Anything to get him into the spotlight so he can make more money on endorsements. Of course these dates never amount to much for Mick...there's no connection beyond the easy sexual conquest, and Mick is getting a bit bored with them if he's honest with himself. One day after a hard off-season workout at the team's facility, he spots a pretty blonde with killer legs wandering around lost looking for the Sabers team offices. After a brief but friendly conversation where Mick directs her where to go, he realizes that the beautiful-in-a-natural-way blonde intrigues him. Enough that he would like to pursue her. And isn't that a first? Mick never has to pursue <i> any woman</i>.<br><br><a href="http://s880.photobucket.com/albums/ac3/aunteecr/?action=view&amp;current=JED-2.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334961i/694117.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Tara Lincoln is a 30-ish, hard-working, fiercely independent single mother of a 14 year-old-son, who owns her own event planning business. Tara's worked hard to overcome her crummy childhood, and her newly established business (The Right Touch) is about to take off. She's not looking for a relationship--men have let her down in the past--she's all about securing the future for her son Nathan and making sure that he doesn't make the same mistakes in his life that she did in hers. But when she meets Mick Riley at the summer team party that her company has planned, she's tempted. Oh, so tempted...He's charming, funny, interesting, and drop-dead <i>gorgeous</i>! And he seems interested in <i>her</i>. Why is that when he could have any woman he wanted?<br><br>Well, I'll say no more. Mick and Tara embark on a relationship, and what a hot, sexy ride it is! Jaci Burton fills the story with plenty of detail, so you know where the characters are coming from and you can understand their actions. There's <i>oodles</i> of juicy hot sex, of course, and there's plenty of wining and dining of (the initially reluctant) Tara by Mick. Tara is introduced to a world that is very foreign to her, one of red carpet events, vacations to exotic beaches (oh, was that a <i>hawt</i> escape), and flights to St. Louis to hang out with Mick's wonderful, loving family, and to watch his professional baseball player brother in action. All the time they spend with each other brings them closer together, yet Tara is constantly waiting for the other shoe to drop, it seems. She knows they come from different worlds, and wonders how once the NFL season starts, if their relationship can last. Do they really have more of a relationship than the "I've-got-to-have-him/her" hot sex? Does Mick want more than just a hot summer fling? And what about her business? Will it start to suffer if she's all wrapped up in Mick? And how about Nathan? Is she shortchanging him if she continues to see Mick? Shouldn't her first priority be her son?<br><br><a href="http://s880.photobucket.com/albums/ac3/aunteecr/?action=view&amp;current=couple2.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334961i/694118.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I have to say I adored Mick. Yes, he had a bit of a womanizing past, put I figured that's just par for the course for a professional athlete. He wasn't perfect (he had a 'secret' that he kept hidden and worried about revealing it to Tara), but he was real. He had a big heart, was great with Tara's son (that alone should've sealed the deal), and was a fantastic, giving lover. He was close to his family, super rich, and gorgeous--what woman <i>wouldn't</i> want him?<br><br>Tara had a bit of a 'this-can't-be-happening-to-me" attitude going on, and who couldn't blame her. She wavered between going all out and giving herself to Mick (and she had no problem on that end--the lady knew what she wanted!) and let the chips fall where they may, to "should-I-protect-my-heart" before it's too late? I could understand her feelings, since Mick had never been in a long-term relationship and she didn't know if he was capable of love. But she did tend to frustrate me a bit. I wanted her to trust Mick and believe in a future with him. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When she got scared/cold feet towards the end of the book, and hurt Mick, I wanted to shake her! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><a href="http://s880.photobucket.com/albums/ac3/aunteecr/?action=view&amp;current=j4-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334962i/694119.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I really enjoyed this story. It had all the elements that I'm looking for in an erotic romance. Besides the extremely hot and well-written love scenes, there was a <i>story</i> here--one that took up three quarters of the book. Plenty of detail, a fast pace with no boring parts, lots of background on the characters and their families, interesting supporting characters, funny dialogue, <i>white hot</i> dialogue, a bit of drama and some angst, a revealing look into the life of a celebrity, and most importantly, likable characters that you can root for.<br><br>If I had one tiny quibble, and this doesn't usually bother me, it was this: Whenever Tara and Mick were intimate, it was always "F*** me, Mick!" Never <i>once</i> did Tara say "Make love to me Mick." <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I know it may sound silly, but that kind of bugged me, especially when the I-love-yous" had been exchanged. At first it didn't matter to me, because Tara was still thinking that the relationship may just be all about the sex, but once you knew their feelings went beyond that...I don't know, I was just kind of waiting for it, and didn't get it. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> But in no way did this mess with my appreciation of the story.<br><br>Fans of (erotic) sports romance, Jaci Burton scored a touchdown with this one. As for the next story in the series (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8192391.Changing_the_Game__Play_by_Play___2_" title="Changing the Game (Play by Play, #2) by Jaci Burton" rel="nofollow noopener">Changing the Game</a>), about Mick's brother and his agent Elizabeth...I dunno, she's going to have to do some creative writing to get me to like that barracuda. She's already dropped some hints that Elizabeth <i>may</i> have a heart beneath that tough shark veneer, but is it enough to make her character likable? I guess we'll have to wait and see. For <b>The Perfect Play</b>? I'll award the extra point and give it <b>5 stars</b>.<br><br><i>Warning: This book contains explicit sex, including oral, (one) anal scene, and a rimming scene; and graphic language. Not for the faint of heart.</i></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="3159668332665411470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer170512642" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15319409764734167564">What an overrated book. Nothing about the story was new or interesting to me. The sex scenes were hot, but if you want to read a hot sex scene, it's just as easy to pick up an erotica, which I'd rather do to be honest. <br/><br/>The story aggravated me on so many levels. It felt like I had fallen into a manufactured after-school special on the dangers of alcohol. I have a teen son and I'm telling you now, he would never be caught dead saying this : <i>I didn't know. I just wanted to be cool like the other gu</i></span>
  <span id="freeText15319409764734167564" style="display:none">What an overrated book. Nothing about the story was new or interesting to me. The sex scenes were hot, but if you want to read a hot sex scene, it's just as easy to pick up an erotica, which I'd rather do to be honest. <br /><br />The story aggravated me on so many levels. It felt like I had fallen into a manufactured after-school special on the dangers of alcohol. I have a teen son and I'm telling you now, he would never be caught dead saying this : <i>I didn't know. I just wanted to be cool like the other guys</i>. It doesn't matter if those are/would be his motives for drinking, he would <i>never</i> say those words out loud, and I'm guessing most teenagers wouldn't either. <br /><br />Also, since when is the "announcement" of someone admitting to be an alcoholic such an earth-shattering moment? I almost expected to hear the faint sounds of a <i>Hallmark Hall of Fame</i> movie in the background. Now, if the guy had admitted he was a raging alcoholic who couldn't stop taking out his anger on people - that might have been another story. But to see a woman get so emotionally worked up because the guy she's dating admitted he partied too much in high school and now he chooses to abstain because he realized he was drinking way too much back then? Give me a <s>fucking</s> break. <br /><br />Please let me disclaimer that I am not taking alcoholism lightly. I have experienced the downfalls of it first hand, as I'm sure many of us have through close friends and family members. This disease can wreck lives. Maybe because I know how much it can wreck lives, I was very disappointed in how ridiculous this particular version of alcoholism seemed like a silly plot device.<br /><br />This is the woman's reaction when she figures out why "Mick" has refused her offers of a drink over the past few weeks. <br /><br /><i>Her throat went dry as the realization of all these weeks together finally fell into focus. But she waited, not asking, knowing it had to come from Mick.<br /><br />"I'm an alcoholic, Tara."<br /><br />The gut punch hurt. She palmed her stomach, was glad she was sitting, because the room spun.<br /><br />"How long?"<br /><br />"Since I was a teenager. Still think I lived a perfect life?"<br /><br />She didn't know if she was angry or hurt, at him or for him.</i><br /><br />Really? A gut punch? A bit melodramatic, I'd say. Now, if she had immediately fessed up to having past issues with people drinking in her life, I would have said...<i>oh yeah, that sucks. No one wants to have to open old wounds</i><br /><br />Oh, but we have to understand because this woman did have her own <s>normal</s> seedy past, and she gave us her own words of <s>"it's okay, most of us have been there and none of us had profound reasons for doing what we did"</s> wisdom. Here's her gem from earlier in the book : <i>By then, I was drinking, doing a few drugs too, anything to numb the pain, you know?</i> Now, I know where the kid gets his lingo from. Apparently, mother and son watched one too many <i>Lifetime</i> movies together.<br /><br />Last complaint. I'm thoroughly sick of every "single mother" story being about a woman who is emotionally unavailable. I'm tired of so many single mom stories painting this bleak picture of someone who has sacrificed 100% for her kids and won't date because their child comes first in every single area of their life. Yet, the person is sad and hollow on the inside, just subconsciously waiting for a man to come and set them free.<br /><br />Usually single moms (again, been there, done that, got the t-shirt) don't date because they don't have a sitter, they're too busy with work, or they don't have the time to go somewhere to meet men. It's not because we <i>don't</i> want to date, or automatically assume that any guy who tries to get close to us is a dead end. I dated here and there when I was a single mom, and was wise enough to keep my dating life separate from my home life until I was seriously involved with someone. I'm guessing most moms are sensible enough to do the same thing.<br /><br />In closing, this book was so not my thing. Why the 2 stars instead of 1? I actually did enjoy a couple of the sex scenes. It wasn't a total fail...<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15319409764734167564" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1149635946" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1149635946" />
    <a title="Didi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6082482-didi"><img alt="Didi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459297426p2/6082482.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1149635946?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Didi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Didi" href="/user/show/6082482-didi">Didi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=library-loan">library-loan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=what-a-jock">what-a-jock</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1149635946" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4419925553429689348">2 STARS<br/><br/>As far as sports romance goes, this was very OKAY. One Night With A Quarterback for example, or even better, The Hook Up by Kristen Callahan, a fave of mine for 2014, were fantastic. This lacked so much for me. First off, I felt there was too much sex. I didn't feel an emotional connection between the hero and heroine till maybe the last 5%. It seemed their relationship was based on sex and hardly more, though I knew they were getting close.<br/>Tara was overly judgmental of Mick when she had </span>
  <span id="freeText4419925553429689348" style="display:none">2 STARS<br /><br />As far as sports romance goes, this was very OKAY. One Night With A Quarterback for example, or even better, The Hook Up by Kristen Callahan, a fave of mine for 2014, were fantastic. This lacked so much for me. First off, I felt there was too much sex. I didn't feel an emotional connection between the hero and heroine till maybe the last 5%. It seemed their relationship was based on sex and hardly more, though I knew they were getting close.<br />Tara was overly judgmental of Mick when she had no reason to be. I understood she was scared and weary, but it was OTT. The scene towards the end at the carnival is a great example. She judged the situation so harshly it was comical when to anyone else it was obvious Mick was oblivious. <br /><br />I know I'm being hard on Tara, but if I don't like the heroine it pretty much ruins the book for me. She didn't want her heart broken again? Sure. But that happened what, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[when she was 15?! To a drugged out, idiotic crackhead? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. News flash, Tara: EVERYONE gets their heart broken as a teenager! Had she felt unworthy or afraid of love because of her upbringing it would have been more believable. In the end, it seemed Tara was looking for a reason to leave Mick.<br /><br />Another of my irritations with Tara was her oddly out of place, take charge attitude in the bedroom. It'd been a long time since she was with anyone, doing anything, but all of a sudden with Mick she became this other woman. My problem wasn't her taking charge but how unlikely that would be considering her lack of experience. She kept declaring when she was going to come, how close she was to coming, how what Mick was doing would make her come, how she wanted to come...it was just out of place and too much. It also blemished Mick's alpha vibe when I would have preferred him to take charge in the bedroom especially with someone who hadn't been with a man in ages. <br /><br />Anyways, this was disappointing and dragged in some places. I started skimming then skipping the sex scenes because once you've read one, you've read them all in this book. The only thing I did like was seeing Mick, the bonafide playboy fall for an average woman and that woman, having had a hard time with life, getting a jackpot in Mick. There was some sweetness and Mick's treatment of Nathan was admirable, therefore this book wasn't a complete bust, so 2 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4419925553429689348" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/920464842?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catarina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catarina" href="/user/show/11538033-catarina">Catarina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11538033-catarina?shelf=is-getting-hot-in-here">is-getting-hot-in-here</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11538033-catarina?shelf=girls-like-athletes">girls-like-athletes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11538033-catarina?shelf=cotton-candy-romance">cotton-candy-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer920464842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17151698711913737226"><b>3,5 Playing Stars.</b><br/><br/>Tara is a single mother, who got pregnant when she was just a teenager and manage to raise her son alone and create her own business. She’s happy alone, or so she thinks. <br/>Enters Mick, famous American Football player, they met at a party she organized and he is immediately taken aback by her. And for the first time he finds himself wanting to pursue a woman. But between being a single mother, his public life and secrets buried in the past, this will probably be the hardest game </span>
  <span id="freeText17151698711913737226" style="display:none"><b>3,5 Playing Stars.</b><br><br>Tara is a single mother, who got pregnant when she was just a teenager and manage to raise her son alone and create her own business. She’s happy alone, or so she thinks. <br>Enters Mick, famous American Football player, they met at a party she organized and he is immediately taken aback by her. And for the first time he finds himself wanting to pursue a woman. But between being a single mother, his public life and secrets buried in the past, this will probably be the hardest game Mick ever had to play. <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420212277i/13190446._SY540_.jpg" width="350" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you want to read a quick, romantic and very steamy book, this a good choice. It wasn’t an unforgettable book and the writing style was sometimes confusing, not to mention that for a book whose plot as a single mother with a teenage son, there wasn’t that much of the son. Nonetheless, it was entertaining and a good series for when you need a “heavy-book-break”. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1402872274i/10002999.jpg" width="350" height="170" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <b>Rating: </b> 3,5 Stars<br> <b>Characters Development: </b> Tara was probably one of the most immature heroines I’ve ever seen. She created drama for no reason at all and saw the bad in everything. For someone who was tried to pass as a strong woman who raised her son alone, she could be worse than a child sometimes. Mick was okay. He was sweet, and sexy and a good guy, but for someone who used to a player (in the non-literal sense of the word) he certainly became a good guy pretty much instantaneously. I really didn’t like Liz, so I don’t know if I want to read the next book, considering is about her. <br> <b>Steam: </b> HOT! <br> <b>Sensible Subjects: </b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br> <b>Love Triangle: </b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>Cheating: </b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br> <b>HEA: </b>	<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yes. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14140241331306176793"><b> 2.5 Stars</b><br/><br/><b>Overall Opinion: </b> Sadly, this kind of fizzled out for me. The beginning sucked me in and had me intruiged, but by the end I was tempted (but didn't) to skim. I got that they had awesome sexual chemistry, but I wanted more than just sex *gasp* --I know. I liked the H. He was great. The h, however, ended up pushing all my buttons -- and definitely <i>not</i> in a good way. She was constantly bringing up other women, even though the H never behaved in any way to deserve that (only hints of a man</span>
  <span id="freeText14140241331306176793" style="display:none"><b> 2.5 Stars</b><br /><br /><b>Overall Opinion: </b> Sadly, this kind of fizzled out for me. The beginning sucked me in and had me intruiged, but by the end I was tempted (but didn't) to skim. I got that they had awesome sexual chemistry, but I wanted more than just sex *gasp* --I know. I liked the H. He was great. The h, however, ended up pushing all my buttons -- and definitely <i>not</i> in a good way. She was constantly bringing up other women, even though the H never behaved in any way to deserve that (only hints of a manwhore past). She also was pushing him away for most of the book. It drove me crazy! I am <i>so</i> grateful that I didn't pay the $7.99 that it is on Amazon and got it through my library instead ;)<br /><br /><b>Brief Summary of the Storyline: </b> This is Tara and Mick's story. They meet at an event that Tara's event planning company put on for his NFL team. They hit it off and end up sharing a steamy night. What Tara didn't expect was for Mick to find her after she snuck out of his hotel room, and for him to pursue a relationship. There is some dancing around each other, but eventually they start dating and fall in love. There is some family and career drama, lots of sexy times, and a few funny moments...and they get a HFN ending.<br /><br /><b>POV:</b> This alternated between focusing on Tara and Mick in 3rd person narrative (not my favorite).<br /><br /><b>Overall Pace of Story: </b> Good until the end (see closure section). I never skimmed and I thought it flowed well.<br /><br /><b>Instalove:</b> No. Instalust? Yes.<br /><br /><b>H rating:</b> 4 stars. Mick. I liked him. He was sweet, loyal, and hot. I really liked how he jumped right in with her son and how he was with his family.<br /><br /><b>h rating:</b> 2 stars. Tara. I appreciated how she seemed to be a good mom and brought herself out of a bad childhood, but her constant pushing away and bringing up other women all the time really irked me.<br /><br /><b>Sadness level: </b>Low. No tissues needed.<br /><br /><b>Push/Pull:</b> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The h is hesitant because their lifestyles are so different. She pushes him away for most of the book. The H pursues the relationship throughout.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Heat level:</b> Moderate/high. There is a good bit of sex in this one. Sometimes it even felt like too much, as I wanted more of a emotional connection between them.<br /><br /><b>Descriptive sex:</b> Yes<br /><br /><b>Safe sex:</b> Yes. Mentions of condoms being used. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[There was mention by the h that she thought she used condoms with her ex, but they were often high or drunk so she wasn't sure. I don't remember any mention of the H's past practices  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>OW/OM drama:</b> No <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Closest is that the H's female agent causes some drama, but it is because she wants better for his career (no romantic feelings)  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Sex scene with OW or OM:</b> No<br /><br /><b>Cheating: </b> No<br /><br /><b>Separation:</b> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[There is a short separation (couple weeks?), and no mention or suggestion of other partners during this separation.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Possible Triggers: </b>Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[H is an alcoholic, brief mention of past drug use by h, and h has child with OM (not present) when she was 15.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Closure: </b>This had one of those endings with the conflict being resolved right before the end. There wasn't even an epilogue, and I think it really would've benefited the story to have one. I'd call it a HFN ending <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[but they do get engaged <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br /><b>How I got it:</b> It was on loan through my public library.<br /><br /><b>Safety:</b> I'd say that this should be <u>Safe</u> for most readers. <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have cheating<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have a descriptive sex scene with OW/OM<br />- <b> Does</b> have the h pushing the H away<br />- <b> Does</b> have a short separation between the h and H<br />- <b> Does Not</b> have abuse<br />- <b> Does Not</b> have OTT sad parts<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have a HEA ending <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_153651872" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/153651872" />
    <a title="Pamela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3007761-pamela"><img alt="Pamela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442454915p2/3007761.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/153651872?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pamela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pamela" href="/user/show/3007761-pamela">Pamela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer153651872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8999115609729363932">4.5/5<br/><br/>First, let's just take a moment to savor this cover. Jed Hill is among the wonders of nature, and I will never grow tired of staring at his absolutely ripped physique. <br/><br/>Fortunately, the book lives up to the cover. Mick is a star quarterback at the height of his career and his carefully orchestrated fame. Tara is an event planner single mom with a 14-year-old son she gave birth to as a teenager. When the two meet at an event Tara plans, neither of them have any idea where they're going to end</span>
  <span id="freeText8999115609729363932" style="display:none">4.5/5<br /><br />First, let's just take a moment to savor this cover. Jed Hill is among the wonders of nature, and I will never grow tired of staring at his absolutely ripped physique. <br /><br />Fortunately, the book lives up to the cover. Mick is a star quarterback at the height of his career and his carefully orchestrated fame. Tara is an event planner single mom with a 14-year-old son she gave birth to as a teenager. When the two meet at an event Tara plans, neither of them have any idea where they're going to end up.<br /><br />Tara doesn't want a parade of men in and out of her life because of the bad example it will set for her son — and because she's never really had any reason to trust men. Her life is her work and her son. (That's something I can relate to!) Mick, on the other hand, is wealthy, famous, a star — but he's sick of the bulimic models and vain starlets his agent has arranged for him to "date."<br /><br />Although this relationship starts in the bedroom — and it gets off to a sexy start, believe me — it quickly becomes more than just sex. Those of you who love erotic love scenes will enjoy the book, because there is a lot of super-scorching sex in this story. But the emotion isn't lacking either, and by the end you'll be delighted, as I was, when Tara opens herself to the possibility of being with Mick and Mick straightens out his priorities, making a firm decision about what matters most to him in life.<br /><br />My only quibble with the book is that I wanted an epilogue. I wanted to see Tara have the family and support she's never had before. Given that the next book involves Gavin, Mick's brother, a pro baseball player, I'm guessing we'll get some of that then. <br /><br />This is the first book I've read on Kindle, so that was an adventure, too.<br /><br />I recommend this to contemporary romance fans, romantica fans, and those who love sports-star heroes.<br /><br />A quick update: A reader friend e-mailed me privately to ask whether there was anal action in the love scenes because she doesn't like to read that. There is. I don't care for that either — just call me Little Miss Vanilla — but as I told her, I found that I was able to just skip a few lines and be fine. It's a great story, and I'd hate her to miss it for that reason.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8999115609729363932" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/210123-d-g?shelf=sports">sports</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/210123-d-g?shelf=snoozefest">snoozefest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/210123-d-g?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/210123-d-g?shelf=will-not-continue-series">will-not-continue-series</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144626301" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11456855213384182814">*2 stars for plot and 1 star for the cover*<br/><br/>This book was the equivalent of a very hot guy who is dumb as a tack - great to look at but boring to listen to.<br/><br/>The problem with the plot was that there was no conflict. It’s basically the story of two people meet, have tons of sex, fall in love, the end. There were a few very small misunderstandings but nothing that would make you bite your nails thinking that they’re not going to make it. All the problems would have been cleared up if the heroine woul</span>
  <span id="freeText11456855213384182814" style="display:none">*2 stars for plot and 1 star for the cover*<br /><br />This book was the equivalent of a very hot guy who is dumb as a tack - great to look at but boring to listen to.<br /><br />The problem with the plot was that there was no conflict. It’s basically the story of two people meet, have tons of sex, fall in love, the end. There were a few very small misunderstandings but nothing that would make you bite your nails thinking that they’re not going to make it. All the problems would have been cleared up if the heroine would have asked the hero one single question but instead she wouldn’t let him get a word and would disappear in a huff. This behavior has put her in the running for "Dumbass Heroine of the Year." <br /><br />Don’t get me wrong, both H/h had some challenge in their lives but neither was relevant to the present because they had already overcome those problems. I don’t want to give any spoilers of the ‘deep, dark, secrets’ (yeah, right!) so I’ll give an example instead. Imagine that you’re reading a book where the heroine is very shy but decides to run for office. Seeing her confront her fear about public speaking, meeting new people, etc. is very different from knowing that she used to be shy but that now she talks in front of crowds all the time. The former makes you sympathize and admire her courage, the latter makes you think “so what?” and that’s the feeling I got reading this book.<br /><br />I did like a few things. The fact that the heroine knew something of sports and that we heard about the hero’s grueling workouts. (Most romance make it seem as if it’s normal for a hero to a get six-pack without exercising.) But that’s about it. The rest was just predictable and boring.<br /><br />So if you want to imagine how it feels to be swept up your feet by a gorgeous, famous, rich man, then this book might be enough for you. If you’re looking for a bit more, then you should skip the book and just look at the cover. Like in the case of a handsome-but-not-so-smart man, it will preserve the illusion that something deep is lurking in that smoldering gaze when in reality, there’s nothing underneath. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11456855213384182814" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16917028560933422050"> ^^THE WAY ME AND THE GUY ON THE COVER PLAYED IN MY HEAD!^^<br/><br/><br/><b>3.5</b><br/><br/>When I see this cover, I think of a few games I could play with Mick. <br/>-Like pin my body parts on his peni….   <span id="freeText16917028560933422050" style="display:none"> ^^THE WAY ME AND THE GUY ON THE COVER PLAYED IN MY HEAD!^^<br /><br /><br /><b>3.5</b><br /><br />When I see this cover, I think of a few games I could play with Mick. <br />-Like pin my body parts on his peni…. I mean body.<br />- A little game of you touch mine and I will touch yours.<br />-Naked touch football, naked twister, naked wrestling Etc<br /><br />You get my point this is one hot cover. Those abs would have me saving money, and hand lotion. I would be doing my laundry on those suckers; it is just one freaking HAWT cover. I am not really into muscles and all that, but I am very into this cover model, and find myself hoping that he would come into…. I mean be into me.<br /><br />Now for the story, I was like ‘Meh’ through it all, I really did enjoy the whole sexy man fall in love with girl next-door type. It gives me hope, that one day some sexy man will come and sweep me off my feet. I can say I enjoyed the book a lot more when they were out of the bedroom.<br /><br />I have always said that something might be wrong with me, cus I am finding the sex between female/male of books to be tiresome. I read it without any interest, and this book was one of those. Just call me crazy, but I think Tara is like the luckiest woman in the world. This woman comes like three times in a row. I sound envious cus I am, just a little bit.<br /><br />Mick I really liked, he seemed like a true genuine character, and as I said really liked the book when they were out of bedroom. I found the sex too plentiful, and tooo odd. By odd I mean, it just felt like they were trying to go too far with it, and then it just sort of fizzled out, by the third sex scene I was pretty much done for. Therefore, I had a hard time with the five-hundred that followed (not that much but you get my meaning). I really like the anal scene, ‘sue me, I love that shit’.<br /><br />This one will be hit with most of GR friends; it was just an ok read for me. I loved learning about football because in reality I could care less. I am considering being a party planner, in reality not the best idea. I loved the whole single mother aspect of the book, as a mother myself I can easily understand the doubts with wanting to get into a relationship. The questions that go with it, will the man accept my child and be respectful. I thought Jaci Burton handled that part splendidly.<br /><br />Overall, liked it just could have done without all the sex.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1789466472" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1789466472" />
    <a title="bella farren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23223005-bella-farren"><img alt="bella farren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598064440p2/23223005.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1789466472?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="bella farren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="bella farren" href="/user/show/23223005-bella-farren">bella farren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23223005-bella-farren?shelf=cliche">cliche</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23223005-bella-farren?shelf=kill-it-with-fire">kill-it-with-fire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23223005-bella-farren?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23223005-bella-farren?shelf=insta-love">insta-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23223005-bella-farren?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1789466472" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10353491867027525249"><b>1.5/5 stars</b><br/><br/>I was a little underwhelmed with this book, I felt like everything lead to one big cliche and nothing was really very original about this book. Many of the characters were cardboard cutouts with no real personality, especially Tara. <br/><br/>Tara was predictably annoying the entire book, the basis for her character was that she was a single mum working to support her teenage son, but for the majority of the book she was either apologising for her son being a burden or burdening him off to othe</span>
  <span id="freeText10353491867027525249" style="display:none"><b>1.5/5 stars</b><br /><br />I was a little underwhelmed with this book, I felt like everything lead to one big cliche and nothing was really very original about this book. Many of the characters were cardboard cutouts with no real personality, especially Tara. <br /><br />Tara was predictably annoying the entire book, the basis for her character was that she was a single mum working to support her teenage son, but for the majority of the book she was either apologising for her son being a burden or burdening him off to other people. <br /><br />That kid spent almost the entire book which spanned across a <i>'summer'</i> sleeping at other people's houses, often so Tara could spent alone time with Mitch <i>(such as a tropical weekend getaway for just the two of them).</i><br /><br />I hate criticising parenting because <b>1)</b> I am most definitely not a parent and I know that you can't really give much of an educated opinion until you've been in that situation and <b>2)</b>, mum shaming has always been a pet-peeve of mine. I don't think she was a "bad" mum in any way, but I think she was built up to be such a selfless character and it missed the mark for me. I found her to be quite self invested and absorbed. <br /><br />I honestly finished this book maybe two hours ago and I've already forgot the majority of what happened. There was no real plot lines apart from the 'romance', which felt fake and annoying. It was more just a pile of sex-scenes and moping characters, rather than a real, exciting romance story that brought out the feels. <br /><br />I was not invested one bit in what happened to the characters, the only people who had real personality were Mick's family, everybody else was predictable. <br /><br />I will definitely not be moving onto the next book because Liz was a character I hated. I didn't hate her decisions but more so that the author than tried to spin her character to just have 'accidentally' been a bitch in her quest to help Mitch's career. I think her motives were never as pure as that, and for the next book to based on her never owning up to her mistakes would kill me inside. <br /><br /><b>edit:</b> I don't mind if there are characters who do bad things, admit them and try to make up for it in one way or another, but Liz was a character who was spun to have just <i>'lost her way'</i> and never really admitted the selfish reason behind it. She was an underhanded and manipulative character who I do <b>not</b> want to read about.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10353491867027525249" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_207419393" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/207419393" />
    <a title="Kristen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5477946-kristen"><img alt="Kristen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312922334p2/5477946.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/207419393?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristen" href="/user/show/5477946-kristen">Kristen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/9807321-the-perfect-play">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=famous-hero">famous-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=playboy-womanizer-manwhore">playboy-womanizer-manwhore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=very-steamy">very-steamy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=sports-romance">sports-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=explicit-content">explicit-content</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=scrumptious-hero">scrumptious-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=fabulous-heroine">fabulous-heroine</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer207419393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10606310326063255929">I love <i>The Perfect Play</i>. It's very erotic, emotional, and captivating. The characters are richly developed and the plot, though somewhat cliché, is engaging and fun to read. I really love this book!<br/><br/>The characters are fantastic and realistic.  Mick and Tara, the hero and heroine, are full of flaws and strengths. I easily believed in their struggles, in their triumphs, and in their relationship. There's enormous chemistry between the two, and I simply couldn't get enough them. <br/><br/>I thoroughly enjoyed</span>
  <span id="freeText10606310326063255929" style="display:none">I love <i>The Perfect Play</i>. It's very erotic, emotional, and captivating. The characters are richly developed and the plot, though somewhat cliché, is engaging and fun to read. I really love this book!<br /><br />The characters are fantastic and realistic.  Mick and Tara, the hero and heroine, are full of flaws and strengths. I easily believed in their struggles, in their triumphs, and in their relationship. There's enormous chemistry between the two, and I simply couldn't get enough them. <br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed Tara's son Nathan. The author captured the essences of a teenage boy. Nathan was delightful and brought many humorous moments to the book.  <br /><br />I especially enjoyed the mother/son dynamic in this book. Tara relationship with Nathan was realistic and poignant. As a single mother, Tara's insecurity and concerns in raising her 14-year-old son alone, brought a vulnerability to her character that made her extremely endearing to me. <br /><br />Mick was fabulous. I fell head-over-heels in love with him. You can't get a more determined, hardworking, protective, refreshingly honest, and sexier than all-get-out hero. He was wonderful to Tara and Nathan, and helped Tera see herself as she truly was. A remarkable woman.   <br /><br />I also love Mick's family. I'm excited we'll get more of them in the next book. They were interesting, well developed, funny, and easy to love characters. Mick's mother, Kathleen, was exceptional for a secondary character. <br /><br />My only compliant-other than Tara sounding like a B-rated porno star during sex scenes-was the ending. It felt abrupt and left the story somewhat hanging. I needed an epilogue. Something to give the story more closure.   <br /><br />Other than that, I love this wonderfully written, extremely erotic, and very endearing love story. <br /><br />Warning: This story is extremely explicit, and at times made me uncomfortable. Read with caution. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10606310326063255929" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781452641577" href="/book/show/17152795-the-perfect-play">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Ezinwanyi by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3916434-mountainkat">MountainKat</a>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4386752-ezinwanyi-chinyere?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4386752-ezinwanyi-chinyere?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4386752-ezinwanyi-chinyere?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1923501389" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8548585930461286418"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456188325ra/18201313.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Aside from this book being uninteresting, I was baffled that two grown-ups were having such simple misunderstandings when they can just text or call each other.<br/><br/>Tara Lincoln was an event planner who was trying to make a name in San Francisco when she landed a huge contract to plan a preseason party for a professional football team. There she met a nice guy Mick Riley and they ended up in bed together. She later finds out that Mick is a quarterback for the professional football team, but they didn</span>
  <span id="freeText8548585930461286418" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456188325ra/18201313.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Aside from this book being uninteresting, I was baffled that two grown-ups were having such simple misunderstandings when they can just text or call each other.<br><br>Tara Lincoln was an event planner who was trying to make a name in San Francisco when she landed a huge contract to plan a preseason party for a professional football team. There she met a nice guy Mick Riley and they ended up in bed together. She later finds out that Mick is a quarterback for the professional football team, but they didn’t really discuss this “thing” being anything more. And that was part of the problem for me. There was very little or unclear communication about anything other than sex and career aspirations. Tara and Mick were good at having sex but discussing life and how to have adult relationships, they were quite juvenile in their actions. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1466770562ra/19517930.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Well, mostly Tara was the annoying character as she was full of assumptions and didn’t give Mick a chance to explain himself. She was just one of those heroines you want to slap. I liked Mick but their relationship seemed so shallow that I wasn’t sure why he would even want to put up with her drama.<br><br>The characters were not developed that well and the writing was so inconsistent for me. The narration made the story worse that I considered quitting on the audiobook several times and just reading the paperback. Honestly, this book was forgettable because there are plenty of better done sports romances with single parents finding love. I will try book 2 before I decide on this series but I will likely not listen to the audio because the narrator’s tone grated my nerves.<br><br><i>I received this audiobook for free from in exchange for an honest review. </i></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susana" href="/user/show/7301000-susana">Susana</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7301000-susana?shelf=erotic">erotic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7301000-susana?shelf=2012">2012</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer431350692" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17170550382084009809">This ended up being, for me, one strange book...<br/>In a way, this is the typical boy meets girl, kind of book....you have one hotshot jocks sport, rich, handsome and altogether a good guy, who suddenly has a change of..."tastes", you might call it...and decides that he's had enough with supermodels and actresses. What he wants now, its a real woman. Good for you, Mick.<br/><br/>Tara is a single working mum, who has placed her romantic life on hold, due to some ghosts of her past, and due to the fact that she</span>
  <span id="freeText17170550382084009809" style="display:none">This ended up being, for me, one strange book...<br />In a way, this is the typical boy meets girl, kind of book....you have one hotshot jocks sport, rich, handsome and altogether a good guy, who suddenly has a change of..."tastes", you might call it...and decides that he's had enough with supermodels and actresses. What he wants now, its a real woman. Good for you, Mick.<br /><br />Tara is a single working mum, who has placed her romantic life on hold, due to some ghosts of her past, and due to the fact that she wants to protect her almost fifteen old son, at any cost..<br />So far, so good.<br />The characters were likeable. Their chemistry believable, and i really liked their dialogues.<br />So what ruined this for me??<br />The sex, too much freaking f*******g sex!! C'mon!<br />So, some people would probably point out, that this an erotic book.<br />FINE!! <br />But most of these scenes weren't erotic, they were just blah and ughhh. It was like the characters had a double personality disorder. You have interesting, level headed people. We get to see their development as characters, and then all of a sudden, they're at it, in a hotel, in the car, in her house, on a plane, on a freaking beach, on his parents house, in his house doing wild monkey <s>love</s> sex...sex, sex...they like one another, but there's no freaking connection!! Its like they're porn stars, who have spend the last decade in a convent or a monastery!! And then there's the language...WTF??? THAT'S SOME seriously foul languague....ALL THE TIME....HONESTLY??? <br />You want to call that sexy???<br />Fine! <br />First time....okay. Second...fifth...tenth time...(eye rolling, while at the same wishing that someone would shut their mouths!)....loosing count: Oh, shut up already!!<br /><br />So while we see their relationship developing, that situation is never transported to what they do behind closed doors...or out in the open in the beach....i just found that strange.<br />And then there's the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[tongue....situation <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>...Don't read the following part, if you're easily embarassed:<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Kissing, and sticking a tongue in the anus ...not sexy, not erotic....just plain, UGH!! And prone to a number of diseases <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />So, for the story, for the romance, i would give this one a solid 3 stars....for the idiocy part it gets a -1.</span>

<div id="review_138837813" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/138837813" />
    <a title="Splage" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4755656-splage"><img alt="Splage" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1371778615p2/4755656.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/138837813?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Splage" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Splage" href="/user/show/4755656-splage">Splage</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4755656-splage?shelf=2011-read">2011-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4755656-splage?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4755656-splage?shelf=hero-big-time-player-man-whore">hero-big-time-player-man-whore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4755656-splage?shelf=sex-erotica-hard-sex">sex-erotica-hard-sex</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4755656-splage?shelf=hero-heroine-famous-person">hero-heroine-famous-person</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4755656-splage?shelf=hot-cover">hot-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4755656-splage?shelf=jealousy">jealousy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4755656-splage?shelf=strong-gentle-hero">strong-gentle-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4755656-splage?shelf=1st-in-series">1st-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4755656-splage?shelf=too-much-sex">too-much-sex</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer138837813" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3781292013042631775">How do I rate this? I think the cover is tainting me because it is the hottest cover ever and because of it I want to say "I really liked it" but, the book wasn't as good. I have read every sports romance I can get my hands on and loved most of them, I would actually call myself a Sports Romance connoisseur. I love the sportsman type, basically man whores with incredible bodies that are easy going and fun loving, but eventually tamed. This book just didn't rank up in my top sport's romance reads</span>
  <span id="freeText3781292013042631775" style="display:none">How do I rate this? I think the cover is tainting me because it is the hottest cover ever and because of it I want to say "I really liked it" but, the book wasn't as good. I have read every sports romance I can get my hands on and loved most of them, I would actually call myself a Sports Romance connoisseur. I love the sportsman type, basically man whores with incredible bodies that are easy going and fun loving, but eventually tamed. This book just didn't rank up in my top sport's romance reads. I definitely liked the book- did I mention the hot cover- and I will read the next in series but, the story just felt forced, predictable and too perfect. I like perfect, but not "too perfect". <p>I did feel a love connection between Mick and Tara and I thought it was cute how their roles were reversed where she just wanted the one night stand unlike him. The were tons of long sex scenes, but the sex seemed awkward, maybe the dialog was just too raw and explicit for the characters. Basically you have a sweet, single mom, event planner that is totally dedicated to her son and business and hasn't been in a relationship good or bad since she was 15 yet, she talked like a hard core porn star when they were intimate. Some of this sex talk was pretty good and was a turn on, but when their love and relationship developed it didn't fit and I cringed a little bit. Also Mick was unbelievably perfect; perfect body, job, family, loved her kid immediately, they gave him one flaw, but he took care of it "perfectly". I wanted him to be a little more rakish and cause a little more conflict. I would call it a paint by numbers romance, it had all the right parts; hot couple, lots of adventuresome sex, bits of glamour, minor conflicts- looks good in the end, but still slightly elementary. </p></span>
  <a data-text-id="3781292013042631775" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1367630739232119743">Soooo, let's just say I got disappointed over this book. I knew like 10% into the book, or less, that <i>The Perfect Play</i> wasn't the perfect book for me. I was too bored, too annoyed over the characters' ways of doing things. I kinda wanted to slap <b>Tara Lincoln</b> (30?) for being so....god what's the word? Naive? Stuck in her own mind? I don't know. I understand that her son come first no matter what, but that doesn't mean you can use him as an excuse, woman. <br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Ready-made family, huh?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><b>Mick </b></span>
  <span id="freeText1367630739232119743" style="display:none">Soooo, let's just say I got disappointed over this book. I knew like 10% into the book, or less, that <i>The Perfect Play</i> wasn't the perfect book for me. I was too bored, too annoyed over the characters' ways of doing things. I kinda wanted to slap <b>Tara Lincoln</b> (30?) for being so....god what's the word? Naive? Stuck in her own mind? I don't know. I understand that her son come first no matter what, but that doesn't mean you can use him as an excuse, woman. <br /><blockquote>

  </b>

Also felt that I didn't really get a connection with the characters. I felt like I was on the outside looking in and the story wasn't all that fascinating to watch. Way too predictable, too lovey-dovey, and worst part was that I felt that <i>insta-love</i> feeling. Though it was more <i>insta-lust</i>, but still... <br /><blockquote>

    <a title="valee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2320890-valee"><img alt="valee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443365004p2/2320890.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer164484499" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9120066752881715956"><b> Why have I not read any comments about this book before!? Seriously guys, I constantly get recommendations but no one recommended this amazing work of art to me and I want you all to know I'm extremely annoyed by that.</b> So now I'll just have to recommend this book to you all, lol, so you don't wait anymore to go and read this freaking amazing book. I just have no words to express how much I adored it. I had been on a reading crises, rating many books with less than 3 stars and just being unable </span>
  <span id="freeText9120066752881715956" style="display:none"><b> Why have I not read any comments about this book before!? Seriously guys, I constantly get recommendations but no one recommended this amazing work of art to me and I want you all to know I'm extremely annoyed by that.</b> So now I'll just have to recommend this book to you all, lol, so you don't wait anymore to go and read this freaking amazing book. I just have no words to express how much I adored it. I had been on a reading crises, rating many books with less than 3 stars and just being unable to find a read that really compelled me. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8341567.The_Perfect_Play__Play_by_Play___1_" title="The Perfect Play (Play by Play, #1) by Jaci Burton" rel="nofollow noopener">The Perfect Play</a> was one of the best books I have read in a while.<br /><br />The characters were amazing, all of them. This is one of those books which actually gives you the whole package: you have family, amazing values, a great alpha hero and a Strong heroine with more than air inside her head. Let's not forget the amazing sexual tension and chemistry between this 2. No bullshit between this two, just a great relationship developing before your eyes. <br /><br />I has such an amazing time with this book. I couldn't put it down and it had been ages since I felt like this with a book in this genre. So if you guys love contemporary romance, this is the book you all have been waiting for. Enjoy.</span>
