<div id="review_139767963" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139767963" />
    <a title="Mandi Schreiner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2704703-mandi-schreiner"><img alt="Mandi Schreiner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368979996p2/2704703.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139767963?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mandi Schreiner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mandi Schreiner" href="/user/show/2704703-mandi-schreiner">Mandi Schreiner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2704703-mandi-schreiner?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139767963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1113652832331812141">Tara Lincoln is an event planner and owner of The Right Touch. By chance, she lands the summer party of the NFL team the San Francisco Sabers. The party is a complete success and it is here she meets the Sabers' star quarterback, Mick Riley. Mick is usually seen with an actress or model draped across his arm, so Tara is shocked when he takes interest in her. He makes her dance with him, and later invites her up to his hotel room.<br/><br/>Mick is tired of his agent Liz throwing beautiful women his way. He</span>
  <span id="freeText1113652832331812141" style="display:none">Tara Lincoln is an event planner and owner of The Right Touch. By chance, she lands the summer party of the NFL team the San Francisco Sabers. The party is a complete success and it is here she meets the Sabers' star quarterback, Mick Riley. Mick is usually seen with an actress or model draped across his arm, so Tara is shocked when he takes interest in her. He makes her dance with him, and later invites her up to his hotel room.<br /><br />Mick is tired of his agent Liz throwing beautiful women his way. He wants someone who is not after his money or fame – and when he sees Tara he instinctively knows she is “normal.” She interests him and he really just wants to get to know her. Being extremely physically attracted to her doesn’t hurt either. <br /><br />Although they are perfect in bed together, real life always throws in more complications. Tara is a single mom, raising a teenager. It has always just been Tara and Nathan and she is not used to putting herself or anyone else first. Mick is known everywhere, and that fame is hard to deal with. Convincing Tara this is not a casual fling will be tough for Mick to do.<br /><br />First let’s all just stare at the cover for The Perfect Play. Sexy, yes? Jaci Burton has been hit with the cover of all covers. I honestly don’t know if I could pass this book up if I saw it sitting on the shelves. *wipes drool*<br /><br />I had a tough start with this book. Mick and Tara meet right at the start of the book, and they had never met before. By page ten, Tara states:<br /><br />"The more time she spent with him, the more she liked him. Dammit. Why couldn’t he be an arrogant son of a bitch, full of himself and talking of nothing by his career and his stats? It would be so much easier to walk away from him if he was self-absorbed. But not only was he gorgeous, he was also funny and was interested in her and her career, and she liked spending time with him.”<br /><br />So Tara knows all this about him by page TEN? Someone she meets on page FOUR. I just don’t think this is a realistic mind set someone would have after just meeting someone. How does she know all of this already? She wouldn’t. And then he takes her up to his hotel room and tells her he is not there to seduce her just to talk and get to know her. Which of course leads to sex. He comes off very pushy to start. Not arrogant as in – hey I’m famous and rich. But arrogant that Tara would naturally choose to be with him. He also assumes right from the beginning that Tara is not out for his money or fame. He makes this assumption without knowing her well enough.<br /><br />So yes, I had a really hard time connecting with Mick at the beginning. but as I continued reading, after a few chapters I felt like the characters calmed down and their relationship took a much nicer turn. I enjoyed Tara’s conflict within herself. She has lived her life always so worried about her son, that just because she meets Mick and does develop feelings for him that doesn’t change who she is. She is still the worried mother. There is one particular scene towards the end where Nathan is used as a ploy, and Tara is hurt by this. And I think this is a great scene because it shows, no matter how much she cares for Mick, Nathan is still the most important thing in her life. She learns to accept other important people, but it really stays true to her character.<br /><br />I really enjoyed the pages spent with Mick back home in St. Louis with his family. This is where I feel we get to meet the real Mick and where the story definitely picks up. Tara is able to see the other side of Mick, the one not playing football or posing for pictures. His brother Gavin and his agent Liz all have some nice scenes as well. <br /><br />One thing I find no fault with are the sex scenes. Yes, look at that cover again – Jaci Burton writes very, very hot smex and the scenes are quite plentiful in this book. The smex scenes do that cover quite proud.<br /><br />I ended up liking this book, it just took me a little while to get there. I believe the next book is about Mick’s brother and baseball star Gavin, and I am very much looking forward to his story.<br /><br />Rating: C+<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1113652832331812141" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_530080724" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/530080724" />
    <a title="Ingie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15589375-ingie"><img alt="Ingie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1477339772p2/15589375.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/530080724?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ingie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ingie" href="/user/show/15589375-ingie">Ingie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15589375-ingie?shelf=books-i-read-2013">books-i-read-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15589375-ingie?shelf=series-new-couples-tbrio">series-new-couples-tbrio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15589375-ingie?shelf=romance-m-f-contemporary">romance-m-f-contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer530080724" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14076305838346132469"><b> Steaming hot, with two lovely protagonists, a good storyline and a good sweet love story.<br/><br/>Like it, 3,5 Stars. </b><br/><br/>We meet <b>the Event Planner Tara</b>. She has herself raised a now teenage son Nathan and she lives for him and her own buisness. She usually don't have time and energy för more than that. At a party, arranged by her for a national (american) football club, she meets <b>the famous football player Mick</b>. He is a playboy and seducer who often appear in the press with beautiful models and actresses. </span>
  <span id="freeText14076305838346132469" style="display:none"><b> Steaming hot, with two lovely protagonists, a good storyline and a good sweet love story.<br><br>Like it, 3,5 Stars. </b><br><br>We meet <b>the Event Planner Tara</b>. She has herself raised a now teenage son Nathan and she lives for him and her own buisness. She usually don't have time and energy för more than that. At a party, arranged by her for a national (american) football club, she meets <b>the famous football player Mick</b>. He is a playboy and seducer who often appear in the press with beautiful models and actresses. Lust and liking arise and after a steamy night in a hotel room, starts a nice described love story. Mick has, perhaps for the first time in his life, to struggle a bit to get the woman, Tara, who he is attracted to. But she is afraid to commit ....<br><br>In my opinion, this is a erotic romance much more than a ordinary contemporary romance. I haven't read as many erotic romances but from my little experience with these, I think this novel had a really good storyline between the bedroom scenes, and I liked it a lot. <br><br><blockquote>
  <a href="http://s1332.photobucket.com/user/Li64/media/Pics/Hotties/jedhill5_zps25908489.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380408737i/799829.jpg" alt=" photo jedhill5_zps25908489.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
  <br>
  <i>Mick (.. or Jed Hill the guy in the pic on the book cover)</i>
</blockquote><br><b>There are a lot of wonderful characters</b> with the hero, heroine, her son and his mother and relatives. Loved them all. It's a bit casual (in a good meaning), it can maybe happen in reality (?) and it's sweet and nicely described. It's a minimal of annoying anxiety, trouble and hurtful acts (thanks!) in the novel. I felt committed to the advancement of the story (besides the too many sex scenes - see below) and I really like to read more parts in the series (new couples and new love stories). <br><br>And, not insignificant, it's so easy to love the gorgeous Mick. No alpha male manners here (Yes, it can get hot and nice even without them!). Plenty of possible husband points for him. What a lovely man!<br><br><b>This story is extremely explicit</b>, and at times it made me (a vanilla girl) a little bit uncomfortable. In my opinion this "buts" would have made the book even better: <br><br>- Maybe some of the bedroom scenes could have been described shorter and less detailed. I as a reader doesn't need to hear every detail, every time they made love with each other. For me, at least, it would have been enough with a hint of what happened sometimes. I don't need to be told everything about the sex between them everytime. I know they could do it in "every possible way". Needless, it was so hot, hot anyway.<br><br>- I don't think Tara's a way to express what she wanted of Mick in the bed matched the description of her personality in general. Fewer <i>F *** Me</i> and instead more loving tender words had raised the level and my feeling for her just then. And maybe Mick's as well? Why not use the nice; <i>Mick, make love to me</i> sometimes?<br><br>Overall; a sweet, hot and lovely story. Will I read moore books in this series? Yes probably.<br><br><b>I Like.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14076305838346132469" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2082263735" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2082263735" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43846663-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574280006p2/43846663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2082263735?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/43846663-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43846663-amanda?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43846663-amanda?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43846663-amanda?shelf=smut">smut</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2082263735" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16262635892949275419"><blockquote>
  <b> “Maybe this was what falling in love was supposed to feel like. Scary and exhilarating at the same time. And maybe it was okay to let it happen.” </b>
</blockquote><br/>To start, I just want to say that I didn’t read <i>The Perfect Play</i> because I thought it was going to be great literature. I read it mainly for the smutty delights which it certainly delivered. <b> Seriously… this is about 60% fucking. </b> I’m not saying that as if it’s a bad thing, it’s just the truth. Overall this was a fun steamy romance with a bit of a</span>
  <span id="freeText16262635892949275419" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b> “Maybe this was what falling in love was supposed to feel like. Scary and exhilarating at the same time. And maybe it was okay to let it happen.” </b>
</blockquote><br />To start, I just want to say that I didn’t read <i>The Perfect Play</i> because I thought it was going to be great literature. I read it mainly for the smutty delights which it certainly delivered. <b> Seriously… this is about 60% fucking. </b> I’m not saying that as if it’s a bad thing, it’s just the truth. Overall this was a fun steamy romance with a bit of a Cinderella feel to it. <br /><br />Mick was the epitome of the almost too good to be true romantic lead. <b>You know the kind… he has perfect abs, tons of money, and can get a woman off 3 times in a row - no problem.</b> While all this is pretty far-fetched as far as real people go, it does make for the ultimate fantasy book boyfriend. I found him to be a really likeable, genuine character. He was another of Jaci Burton’s male leads that doesn’t objectify women. You never hear him demean a woman and he truly respects Tara’s career. There were some great scenes between him and Nathan where he really stepped up to the plate and became a male role model, if not father figure, for Nathan. <br /><br />Speaking of which, I also really liked Nathan. The only thing I wish there was more of was an exploration of the mother son relationship. They just didn’t seem all that close which is a bit odd considering she’s a single parent and Nathan isn’t an awful kid. I would think they would have a somewhat closer relationship than what I read. I would have really liked to see them be friendlier with each other I suppose. <br /><br />I like that Tara had her own career and worked hard to get to where she is today. She wasn’t a sob story requiring pity. She doesn’t go around going “woe is me” all the time. She’s a fighter and I respected her a great deal for that. However, I did find her a little bland personality wise. Tara is so distrustful of Mick for no reason. She just knee jerk assumes he’s an asshole after he’s done nothing but be kind and amazing to her. It’s drama for the sake of drama. Mick is similar in his treatment of Liz. Yes, Liz screwed things up but he refuses to see anything other than what he has deemed deplorable about her. It’s like none of the other times she’s probably helped him or acted as a friend mattered. I know he’s acting in anger but it’s pretty short sighted and petty. So for this odd personality trait maybe they are perfect for each other. <br /><br /><i>The Perfect Play</i> is a quick steamy read. I would not recommend it for someone who is looking for an amazing story with really complex characters. This is the perfect book for someone looking for a fun steamy romance with a side of grade-A smut. I liked the characters and I wanted them to have a HEA and would read another book featuring them. <br /><br /><b>P.S.</b> I just found out that the next book in this series, <i>The Final Score</i>, will feature an all grown up Nathan! I want that book so bad!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16262635892949275419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YvgK6kwMOpUM3KyzD5gGxHfHMyLP+nnZuVinECLp2QCbY3XjGSZTtmB4QGsEktSsSL8f/ykX4nNY7lhxIFHhog==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lVfTk+/nXds/vOvllApSt84jIflteyzVrfTKfmDiK3dszKyaus00+FMYBz2fAIDf8VsNJIuWt39MQjUfYloT1Q==')})
  }
